## MANDATORY: Use Sourcegraph Code Search Tools BEFORE Any Code Changes

You have Sourcegraph MCP tools available (keyword_search, nls_search, list_files, read_file, go_to_definition, find_references, deepsearch, deepsearch_read). You MUST use them as your primary code discovery method.

Use `list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.

**CRITICAL — TWO-PHASE WORKFLOW:**

### Phase 1: Search & Understand (MANDATORY — DO NOT SKIP)
BEFORE writing ANY code, modifying ANY file, or running ANY implementation command, you MUST:
1. Read the task instructions and identify key functions, classes, files, or concepts mentioned
2. Make at least 3 Sourcegraph search calls to find and understand the relevant code:
   - Use `keyword_search` with the repo filter to find specific symbols/identifiers from the task
   - Use `list_files` to understand the project structure
   - Use `go_to_definition` / `find_references` to trace code relationships
3. DO NOT start implementing until you have searched for the key terms from the task
5. Use `deepsearch` for dependency/impact analysis — understand blast radius of changes, find callers of modified functions, downstream consumers of changed interfaces, and tests covering affected code paths
6. `deepsearch` returns a polling link, NOT immediate results. After calling it, continue working with other tools for 30-60 seconds, then call `deepsearch_read` with the polling link
7. Retry `deepsearch_read` at least 3 times — Deep Search takes 50-120 seconds to complete
8. For code review tasks: the PR diff alone does NOT show full impact. Use `deepsearch` to find what else depends on the changed code before finalizing your review

### Phase 2: Implement
After understanding the codebase through Sourcegraph:
1. Use Read to verify local file contents (Sourcegraph indexes latest branch, local may differ)
2. If Sourcegraph shows different code than local, TRUST THE LOCAL CODE
3. Make your code changes — stop searching, focus on implementation

See CLAUDE.md for the complete tool selection guide.

# [VS Code] Fix Stale TypeScript Diagnostics After Git Branch Switch

**Repository:** microsoft/vscode  
**Difficulty:** HARD  
**Category:** big_code_feature
**Task Type:** Feature Implementation - Large Codebase

**Reference:** [Trevor's Big Code Research](../../../docs/TREVOR_RESEARCH_DEC2025.md#1-vs-code-stale-diagnostics-after-git-branch-switch)

## Description

Users are seeing stale TypeScript diagnostics in the Problems panel after switching Git branches. Files that no longer have errors still show the old errors until the user manually opens each file and makes an edit. It seems like the diagnostics pipeline only refreshes on in-editor changes and misses file-on-disk changes from Git operations.

## Task

This task requires implementing code changes to fix stale diagnostics.

### Required Implementation

Check the full diagnostics flow from a text change through the extension host to the Problems view, identify where file system changes should trigger diagnostic updates, and propose where we'd need to add listeners to fix this.

### Implementation Steps

1. **Understand the diagnostics pipeline**:
   - Find the main diagnostics collection and how it stores errors per file
   - Locate the extension host communication for sending diagnostics to the client
   - Find the Problems view panel and how it subscribes to diagnostics
   - Look for existing file change listeners (e.g., `deleteAllDiagnosticsInFile`, `onWillChange`)

2. **Identify where diagnostics are currently refreshed**:
   - Find the text change event handlers that trigger re-diagnostics
   - Understand how the diagnostics pipeline reacts to document changes
   - Look for any existing file system watchers or listeners

3. **Add file system change triggers**:
   - Add listener for file changes on disk (e.g., from `git checkout`)
   - Trigger diagnostics refresh for changed files
   - Clear stale diagnostics for files that no longer exist
   - Re-run TypeScript/language server analysis for affected files

4. **Test the fix**:
   - Switch branches that change TypeScript errors
   - Verify stale diagnostics are cleared
   - Verify new errors are shown after branch switch
   - No duplicate diagnostics appear

5. **Verify no regressions**:
   - All tests pass: `npm test`
   - No performance regression from additional file watchers
   - Diagnostics still work for in-editor changes

## Success Criteria

[x] Stale diagnostics are cleared when files change on disk  
[x] New diagnostics appear after Git branch switch  
[x] Diagnostics refresh without requiring manual file edits  
[x] Problems panel reflects current state of files  
[x] All tests pass: `npm test`  
[x] No performance regression  
[x] Code follows VS Code conventions and patterns  

## Testing

```bash
npm test
```

import assert from 'assert';
import { URI } from '../../../../../base/common/uri.js';
import { IMarker, MarkerSeverity, IRelatedInformation } from '../../../../../platform/markers/common/markers.js';
import { MarkersModel, Marker, ResourceMarkers, RelatedInformation } from '../../browser/markersModel.js';
import { groupBy } from '../../../../../base/common/collections.js';
import { ensureNoDisposablesAreLeakedInTestSuite } from '../../../../../base/test/common/utils.js';

class TestMarkersModel extends MarkersModel {

	constructor(markers: IMarker[]) {
		super();

		const byResource = groupBy(markers, r => r.resource.toString());

		Object.keys(byResource).forEach(key => {
			const markers = byResource[key];
			if (markers) {
				const resource = markers[0].resource;

				this.setResourceMarkers([[resource, markers]]);
			}
		});
	}
}

suite('MarkersModel Test', () => {

	ensureNoDisposablesAreLeakedInTestSuite();

		const testObject = new TestMarkersModel([marker1, marker2, marker3, marker4]);
		const actuals = testObject.resourceMarkers[0].markers;

		assert.strictEqual(actuals.length, 4);
		assert.notStrictEqual(actuals[0].id, actuals[1].id);

import assert from 'assert';
import { URI } from '../../../../base/common/uri.js';

import { IMarkerData, MarkerSeverity } from '../../common/markers.js';

function randomMarkerData(severity = MarkerSeverity.Error): IMarkerData {
	return {
		severity,
		message: Math.random().toString(16),
		startLineNumber: 1,

@extHostNamedCustomer(MainContext.MainThreadDiagnostics)
export class MainThreadDiagnostics implements MainThreadDiagnosticsShape {

	private readonly _activeOwners = new Set<string>();

	private readonly _proxy: ExtHostDiagnosticsShape;
	private readonly _markerListener: IDisposable;

	constructor(
		extHostContext: IExtHostContext,
		@IMarkerService private readonly _markerService: IMarkerService,
		@IUriIdentityService private readonly _uriIdentService: IUriIdentityService,
	) {
		this._proxy = extHostContext.getProxy(ExtHostContext.ExtHostDiagnostics);

		this._markerListener = this._markerService.onMarkerChanged(this._forwardMarkers, this);
	}

	dispose(): void {
		this._markerListener.dispose();
		this._activeOwners.forEach(owner => this._markerService.changeAll(owner, []));
		this._activeOwners.clear();
	}

	private _forwardMarkers(resources: readonly URI[]): void {
		const

type ScriptKind = 'TS' | 'TSX' | 'JS' | 'JSX';

function mode2ScriptKind(mode: string): ScriptKind | undefined {
	switch (mode) {
		case languageModeIds.typescript: return 'TS';
		case languageModeIds.typescriptreact: return 'TSX';
		case languageModeIds.javascript: return 'JS';
		case languageModeIds.javascriptreact: return 'JSX';
	}
	return undefined;
}

}

212-assistanttext-
Now let me understand the broader structure. The key insight is:

1. **Extension host side** (`extHostDiagnostics.ts`): Extensions (like TypeScript) create `DiagnosticCollection`s and set diagnostics via the extension API
2. **Main thread side** (`mainThreadDiagnostics.ts`): Receives diagnostic changes from extension host, stores them in `IMarkerService`
3. **TypeScript extension** (`bufferSyncSupport.ts`): The TS extension only requests diagnostics for open/visible documents and reacts to text document changes
4. **Problem**: When git switches branches, files change on disk but the TS extension doesn't know about it. The `onDidChangeTextDocument` only fires for in-editor changes.

The fix should be in `bufferSyncSupport.ts` - we need to listen for file system changes from `vscode.workspace.onDidChangeFile` (the `FileSystemWatcher`) and trigger diagnostic refresh for affected files.

Let me look at how the TypeScript extension already handles file changes:

223-assistanttext-
Now let me understand the fix clearly:

**Root cause**: When git switches branches, files change on disk. The TypeScript language server extension (`bufferSyncSupport.ts`) only reacts to `onDidChangeTextDocument` (in-editor changes) and `onDidChangeVisibleTextEditors`. It does NOT listen for disk-level file changes (`vscode.workspace.createFileSystemWatcher`). So when git changes files on disk, the TS server still has old file content and old diagnostics persist.

**Fix location**: `bufferSyncSupport.ts` - In the `listen()` method, we need to add a `FileSystemWatcher` that watches for file changes and triggers diagnostic refresh for synced buffers whose files changed on disk.

Let me first restore all the emptied files from git, then add the fix.

/*---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
 *  Copyright (c) Microsoft Corporation. All rights reserved.
 *  Licensed under the MIT License. See License.txt in the project root for license information.
 *--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------*/

import * as vscode from 'vscode';
import { isWeb } from '../utils/platform';

export const file = 'file';
export const untitled = 'untitled';
export const git = 'git';
export const github = 'github';
export const azurerepos = 'azurerepos';

/** Live share scheme */
export const vsls = 'vsls';
export const walkThroughSnippet = 'walkThroughSnippet';
export const vscodeNotebookCell = 'vscode-notebook-cell';
export const officeScript = 'office-script';

/** Used for code blocks in chat by vs code core */
export const chatCodeBlock = 'vscode-chat-code-block';

export function getSemanticSupportedSchemes() {
	const alwaysSupportedSchemes = [
		untitled,
		walkThroughSnippet,
		vscodeNotebookCell,
		chatCodeBlock,
	];

	if (isWeb()) {
		return [
			...(vscode.workspace.workspaceFolders ?? []).map(folder => folder.uri.scheme),
			...alwaysSupportedSchemes,
		];
	}

	return [
		file,
		...alwaysSupportedSchemes,
	];
}

/**
 * File scheme for which JS/TS language feature should be disabled
 */
export const disabledSchemes = new Set([
	git,
	vsls,
	github,
	azurerepos,
]);

export function isOfScheme(uri: vscode.Uri, ...schemes: string[]): boolean {
	const normalizedUriScheme = uri.scheme.toLowerCase();
	return schemes.some(scheme => normalizedUriScheme === scheme);
}
253-assistanttext-
Now I need to understand the key point: when Git switches branches, files on disk change. The `vscode.workspace.createFileSystemWatcher` can detect these changes. When a file changes on disk that has a synced buffer, we need to:

1. Re-open the buffer with the new content (so the TS server gets the updated content)
2. Request fresh diagnostics

Let me now implement the fix. The approach is to add a file system watcher in the `listen()` method that watches for `**/*.{ts,tsx,js,jsx}` files and triggers a diagnostic refresh when files change on disk.

256-assistanttext-
Now let me implement the fix. The key change is in `bufferSyncSupport.ts`'s `listen()` method. We need to:

1. Create a file system watcher for TS/JS files
2. When a file changes on disk, check if it has a synced buffer
3. If it does, re-open the buffer with new content and request diagnostics
4. If a file is deleted, close the resource and clear its diagnostics

        "+          }",
        "+        }",
        "+      }",
        "+    });",
        "   }",
        " ",
        "   dispose(): void {",
        "     this._markerListener.dispose();",
        "+    this._fileChangeListener.dispose();",
        "     this._activeOwners.forEach(owner => this._markerService.changeAll(owner, []));",
        "     this._activeOwners.clear();",
        "   }"

1. EDIT /workspace/extensions/typescript-language-features/src/tsServer/bufferSyncSupport.ts
Before
	public listen(): void {
		if (this.listening) {
			return;
		}
		this.listening = true;
		vscode.workspace.onDidOpenTextDocument(this.openTextDocument, this, this._disposables);
		vscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(this.onDidCloseTextDocument, this, this._disposables);
		vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(this.onDidChangeTextDocument, this, this._disposables);
		vscode.window.onDidChangeVisibleTextEditors(e => {
			for (const { document } of e) {
				const syncedBuffer = this.syncedBuffers.get(document.uri);
				if (syncedBuffer) {
					this.requestDiagnostic(syncedBuffer);
				}
			}
		}, this, this._disposables);
		vscode.workspace.textDocuments.forEach(this.openTextDocument, this);
	}
After
	public listen(): void {
		if (this.listening) {
			return;
		}
		this.listening = true;
		vscode.workspace.onDidOpenTextDocument(this.openTextDocument, this, this._disposables);
		vscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(this.onDidCloseTextDocument, this, this._disposables);
		vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(this.onDidChangeTextDocument, this, this._disposables);
		vscode.window.onDidChangeVisibleTextEditors(e => {
			for (const { document } of e) {
				const syncedBuffer = this.syncedBuffers.get(document.uri);
				if (syncedBuffer) {
					this.requestDiagnostic(syncedBuffer);
				}
			}
		}, this, this._disposables);
		vscode.workspace.textDocuments.forEach(this.openTextDocument, this);

		// Watch for file changes on disk (e.g. from git branch switches) to refresh diagnostics
		const fileWatcher = vscode.workspace.createFileSystemWatcher('**/*.{ts,tsx,js,jsx}');
		this._disposables.push(fileWatcher);
		fileWatcher.onDidChange(uri => {
			this.onDiskFileChanged(uri);
		}, this, this._disposables);
		fileWatcher.onDidCreate(uri => {
			this.onDiskFileChanged(uri);
		}, this, this._disposables);
		fileWatcher.onDidDelete(uri => {
			this.onDiskFileDeleted(uri);
		}, this, this._disposables);
	}

	private onDiskFileChanged(uri: vscode.Uri): void {
		const syncedBuffer = this.syncedBuffers.get(uri);
		if (syncedBuffer) {
			// Re-open the buffer so the TS server picks up the new content from disk
			syncedBuffer.open();
			this.requestDiagnostic(syncedBuffer);
		}
	}

	private onDiskFileDeleted(uri: vscode.Uri): void {
		const syncedBuffer = this.syncedBuffers.get(uri);
		if (syncedBuffer) {
			this.closeResource(uri);
		}
	}
2. EDIT /workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.ts
Before
import { IMarkerService, IMarkerData } from '../../../platform/markers/common/markers.js';
import { URI, UriComponents } from '../../../base/common/uri.js';
import { MainThreadDiagnosticsShape, MainContext, ExtHostDiagnosticsShape, ExtHostContext } from '../common/extHost.protocol.js';
import { extHostNamedCustomer, IExtHostContext } from '../../services/extensions/common/extHostCustomers.js';
import { IDisposable } from '../../../base/common/lifecycle.js';
import { IUriIdentityService } from '../../../platform/uriIdentity/common/uriIdentity.js';

@extHostNamedCustomer(MainContext.MainThreadDiagnostics)
export class MainThreadDiagnostics implements MainThreadDiagnosticsShape {

	private readonly _activeOwners = new Set<string>();

	private readonly _proxy: ExtHostDiagnosticsShape;
	private readonly _markerListener: IDisposable;

	constructor(
		extHostContext: IExtHostContext,
		@IMarkerService private readonly _markerService: IMarkerService,
		@IUriIdentityService private readonly _uriIdentService: IUriIdentityService,
	) {
		this._proxy = extHostContext.getProxy(ExtHostContext.ExtHostDiagnostics);

		this._markerListener = this._markerService.onMarkerChanged(this._forwardMarkers, this);
	}

	dispose(): void {
		this._markerListener.dispose();
		this._activeOwners.forEach(owner => this._markerService.changeAll(owner, []));
		this._activeOwners.clear();
	}
After
import { IMarkerService, IMarkerData } from '../../../platform/markers/common/markers.js';
import { URI, UriComponents } from '../../../base/common/uri.js';
import { MainThreadDiagnosticsShape, MainContext, ExtHostDiagnosticsShape, ExtHostContext } from '../common/extHost.protocol.js';
import { extHostNamedCustomer, IExtHostContext } from '../../services/extensions/common/extHostCustomers.js';
import { IDisposable } from '../../../base/common/lifecycle.js';
import { IUriIdentityService } from '../../../platform/uriIdentity/common/uriIdentity.js';
import { IFileService, FileChangeType } from '../../../platform/files/common/files.js';

@extHostNamedCustomer(MainContext.MainThreadDiagnostics)
export class MainThreadDiagnostics implements MainThreadDiagnosticsShape {

	private readonly _activeOwners = new Set<string>();

	private readonly _proxy: ExtHostDiagnosticsShape;
	private readonly _markerListener: IDisposable;
	private readonly _fileChangeListener: IDisposable;

	constructor(
		extHostContext: IExtHostContext,

3. EDIT /workspace/src/vs/workbench/api/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.ts
Before
import { IMarkerService, IMarkerData } from '../../../platform/markers/common/markers.js';
import { URI, UriComponents } from '../../../base/common/uri.js';
import { MainThreadDiagnosticsShape, MainContext, ExtHostDiagnosticsShape, ExtHostContext } from '../common/extHost.protocol.js';
import { extHostNamedCustomer, IExtHostContext } from '../../services/extensions/common/extHostCustomers.js';
import { IDisposable } from '../../../base/common/lifecycle.js';
import { IUriIdentityService } from '../../../platform/uriIdentity/common/uriIdentity.js';

@extHostNamedCustomer(MainContext.MainThreadDiagnostics)
export class MainThreadDiagnostics implements MainThreadDiagnosticsShape {

	private readonly _activeOwners = new Set<string>();

	private readonly _proxy: ExtHostDiagnosticsShape;
	private readonly _markerListener: IDisposable;

	constructor(
		extHostContext: IExtHostContext,
		@IMarkerService private readonly _markerService: IMarkerService,
		@IUriIdentityService private readonly _uriIdentService: IUriIdentityService,
	) {
		this._proxy = extHostContext.getProxy(ExtHostContext.ExtHostDiagnostics);

		this._markerListener = this._markerService.onMarkerChanged(this._forwardMarkers, this);
	}

	dispose(): void {
		this._markerListener.dispose();
		this._activeOwners.forEach(owner => this._markerService.changeAll(owner, []));
		this._activeOwners.clear();
	}
